## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Materials Science / Constitutive Modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the thermomechanical response of solid materials, focusing on how stress evolves with strain under varying temperatures. It typically involves constitutive equations describing elastic-plastic deformation, strain hardening, and thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke-Thermal law: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elastic response with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (plastic flow stress with thermal softening factor)
- Johnson-Cook separable form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (multiplicative decomposition of strain hardening and temperature effects)
- Logarithmic strain hardening: sigma = c0 * log(1 + c1 * epsilon) * (1 + c2 * T) (dislocation cell structure evolution at large strains)
- Offset plastic strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (accounting for yield strain offset in plastic deformation)
- Saturation flow stress: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (1 + c2 * T) (stress approaching steady-state value under large deformation)
- Rational softening model: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * epsilon) * (1 + c2 * T) (empirical stress-strain curve with bounded hardening)
- Thermomechanical polynomial: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 + c3 * T + c4 * epsilon * T (Taylor expansion of constitutive surface for coupled effects)
- Additive athermal-thermal split: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * exp(c3 * T) (separating strain-driven athermal resistance from thermally activated softening)
- Square-root Taylor hardening: sigma = c0 * sqrt(epsilon + c1) * (1 + c2 * T) (dislocation density scaling with accumulated plastic strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Dislocation density scaling → Square-root dependence sqrt(c * epsilon) or fractional power epsilon**0.5 (Taylor hardening theory)
- Thermally activated yield → Exponential temperature dependence in additive split f(epsilon) + c0 * exp(c1 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal barrier overcoming)
- Elastic-plastic yielding → Strain offset (epsilon + c)**n capturing elastic limit and plastic onset
- Logarithmic strain hardening → log(1 + c * epsilon) capturing dislocation cell structure evolution
- Fully coupled thermomechanical response → Separable product form f(epsilon) * g(T) assuming temperature scales flow stress uniformly
- Nonlinear elasticity/finite strain → Logarithmic or rational mappings of strain to stress for large deformations
- Thermal modulus degradation → Linear temperature scaling of stiffness c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*(T - c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)`
Given the numerical values `c1 = 3.0`, `c4 = 3.0`, and `c3 = c6 = 308.8646781296164`, we can simplify the GT algebraically:
`GT = c0*epsilon**3 - c2*(T - c3) + c5*epsilon**3*(T - c3)`
`GT = c0*epsilon**3 - c2*T + c2*c3 + c5*epsilon**3*T - c5*c3*epsilon**3`
Grouping by basis functions:
`GT = (c5)*T*epsilon**3 + (-c2)*T + (c0 - c5*c3)*epsilon**3 + (c2*c3)*1`
**Required Basis Functions:** `{1, T, epsilon**3, T*epsilon**3}`
Any valid candidate must be expressible as a linear combination of these four basis functions. Extra terms must be zeroable via free constants, and missing basis functions make a candidate invalid.

Candidate 18 (with c2=0): `(c0*c1)*T*epsilon**3 + c0*T + c3*epsilon**3 + c4`

- c0*c1 = 8.63802815432207 (coefficient of T*epsilon**3)
- c0 = -0.39029568781474044 (coefficient of T)
- c3 = (4.255830478818137 - 8.63802815432207*308.8646781296164) (coefficient of epsilon**3)
- c4 = 0.39029568781474044*308.8646781296164 (constant)

From c0 = -0.39029568781474044, c1 = 8.63802815432207/(-0.39029568781474044) ≈ -22.13...

All constants can be freely chosen. **This matches!**
